text:
With no disrespect to other reviewers who had a variety of issues and criticisms with this recipe, it occurs to me that either they are too familiar with boxed yellow cake, or are unfamiliar with basic, scratch, cake making techniques. True, boxed yellow cake is more moist, but it tastes, well, like boxed cake mix, which is unmistakable and just plain bad. True, scratch butter cakes can have a tendency to be a little dry, particularly yellow butter cakes.  But this yellow cake is definitely better than any I have ever tried in my 50 years of baking--more moist than most, flavorful, and with a light and tender crumb. Cream your butter and sugar well, a good few minutes.  This is key for a light and fluffy cake! Follow the recipe directions carefully--add yolks one at a time, blending well after each addition. Add the flour and milk separately and with a light hand, beginning and ending with the flour. And do not overbake! If your cake is dry or dense you are not following the directions. I made half a recipe in an 8x8" pan and frosted it with half a recipe of "Buttercream Icing." I challenge you to find a better yellow cake with buttercream frosting in any well-respected neighborhood bakery, or in any old-fashioned baker's recipe box!

text:
This is the BEST yellow cake recipe there is.My search ends here.The only difference that i did was to take away 2tbsps of the regular AP flour in each cup and substitute it with 2tbsps of cornstarch as suggested by another reviewer.I did this as i didnt have any cake flour on hand.The cake came out moist,fluffy and delish.Beats a boxed mix anyday.
As a tip for new bakers like myself:
1.Absolutely do sift the flour and baking powders twice for maximum integration.
2.Do beat the yolks one by one ,it adds to the fluffiness.
3.Once the batter is poured into the pan,tap the pan a few times on top of the counter so that batter will spread evenly and rise evenly.

After trying this recipe for the first time I found it a little dry, dense, and eggy, so I experimented with it to change the flavor and texture. I used 5 eggs, 3 whole eggs, 2 egg yolks, I added 1/2 cup more flour(all purpose), instead of 3/4 c milk I used 1 1/4 cup low-fat buttermilk (to make more moist). After making these few adjustments my cakes come out just the way I like them Good!

text:
I've used this recipe several times now after experimenting with some other yellow cake recipes found on this site.  This is by far the moistest, most delicious homemade yellow cake I've ever baked, and I bake a lot.  I took a suggestion from other reviewers and used 4 yolks and 2 whole eggs.  I've baked it in all forms: cupcakes(1/2 full about 15 min), 2 9" rounds (20-21 min), 9x13 (30 min) and it always comes out amazingly.  For those people having problems with your cake sinking--check your baking powder and make sure it is fresh.  Old/stale baking powder is the prime cause of cakes sinking.  Just want to send a big THANK YOU to David for sharing such a wonderful recipe!

I've made this cake several times and I think it's so moist that I like to eat it without any icing on it at all.  It is not dry as others have stated.  If you think it's too dry you're either not measuring the ingredients properly, not using the ingredients stated in the recipe, or you're overbaking the cake.  Use a toothpick to test if the cake is done.  Touching the top of the cake to see if it springs back isn't as a reliable test for doneness with this cake.

text:
The cake does smell and taste eggy when it first comes out of the oven but when it cools off the eggy taste goes away.  An angel food cake is the same way.  If you eat a piece of it while it's still slightly warm it will taste eggy.  After it's cooled off the eggy taste goes away. If the cake comes out dry it means you're baking it too long.  Watch for the cake to rise up in the middle and then deflate slightly.  It's at this point you should to see if the cake is done.  If a toothpick inserted in the middle of the cake comes out with wet batter then give cake about 5 more minutes and check it again.  If the toothpick comes out with gummy batter on it then give it about 3 more minutes.  If it comes out with a few crumbs sticking to it then it's done.  If it comes out perfectly clean then it's definitely done and may in fact be overdone.  I'd also like to add that if you're going to change any of the ingredients in this recipe then you shouldn't expect it to come out right.  Changing the ingredients and then giving a poor review is unfair to the person who submitted the recipe.

text:
I've now used this recipe several times and it just gets better and better!  I didn't want to use 8 egg yolks and essentially waste the whites so I modified this recipe and made a white cake by using 4 whole eggs instead.  I read the other reviews and was nervous that this scratch cake recipe wouldn't taste good, because I thought it would be dry.  Using NAPLES advice, I was sure to cream my butter and sugar together for a long time.  I first cut my butter into 1/2 inch pats, creamed that.  I then added sugar in about 1/4 cup increments (guessing) and creamed that until my sugar and butter looked light and fluffy.  I added one egg at a time scraping down the sides after each time.  I turned my mixer off and stirred in my vanilla extract.  I started and ended with my sifted flour mixture and added the milk in 2 parts while the flour mixture took 3 parts.  In the end, it was light and fluffy (truly, the batter looked gorgeous) and I've made cupcakes every time.  I only bake for about 13-15 minutes and I have the perfect cupcake.  JDSIMON/DAVE - this recipe is a true winner!

text:
I have made a lot of cakes in my life -- always searching for a good one.  This is it.  It has a wonderful flavor and texture.  Not too dense, not to spongey.  As others mentioned, be sure to beat the butter and sugar together well.  Then, beat well after adding each egg yolk.  For baking, I set the timer for 20 minutes and watched it carefully -- pulling it out when it bounced back a bit when pressed in the center.  Don't let the top and edges get browned because then it will be dry.  I think this is the best cake I've ever made.  I highly recommend it.

text:
This is a great cake recipe. The way a classic yellow cake should taste, possibly better. If a box mix cake is what you are hoping to get, you should probably stick with the box, which is filled with all kinds of ingredients and chemicals that you just won't find in a real homemade quality cake like this recipe. I cut the recipe in half and made cupcakes with it. They came out light and flavorful and moist with a delicate crumb. As another reviewer stated, take the time to really cream your butter and sugar in the beginning, adding yolks one at a time and beating thoroughly. This, plus sifting the flour and baking powder and salt, really makes a difference in texture. When alternating the flour mixture with the milk, start and end with flour, splitting the flour into thirds and the milk in half. This will ensure everything is incorporated and will help prevent over mixing, which will make the cake tough and dry. Try this recipe, it's SO delicious!

text:
I bake everything from scratch, and I've made many yellow cake recipes - this one is by far my favorite! It is incredibly moist, and yellow cakes usually aren't. (Unless you buy those chock-full-o'-chemicals box mixes - yuck!) The crumb on this cake is almost a sticky kind of moist, and it is beyond flavorful.  You DO need to follow the directions carefully, though - and you have to use the exact ingredients for which the recipe calls. If you blanch at the idea of using eight full egg yolks in a cake recipe or you can't be bothered to get *cake* flour, don't be surprised if the cake isn't as good as you'd hoped. In my opinion, a stand mixer is a must in order to cream the butter and sugar to the proper loft and sufficiently beat the eggs to build up the protein strands in the eggs to give the batter enough structure. The dry ingredients should be mixed *just* enough to incorporate, and not a minute more. I made this recipe as cupcakes for my daughter (whose favorite color is yellow and thus wanted as much yellow for her birthday as she could get her paws on!), and everyone - adults and children alike - swooned for these.  Follow the directions faithfully and you will have a yellow cake to die for!

text:
Tried this for the first time for my daughter's birthday cake and it turned out perfect. Everyone loved it! I'm not sure how anyone could rate this recipe negatively, but I have a feeling they missed one of the following keys to baking from scratch:
* ALL ingredients (eggs, butter, milk especially) MUST be at room temperature
* Cream the butter and sugar until it's really fluffy (this takes patience)
* SLOWLY mix in one yolk at a time, barely blending
* SIFT all of the dry ingredients.
* SLOWLY mix in a small amount (about a third) of the flour, blending completely. Then about a third of the milk, blending completely. Repeat until all flour and milk is gone.

I also made my own cake flour by measuring out 2 cups of all-purpose flour, removing 4 Tbsp, replacing it with 4 Tbsp of cornstarch, then sifting the mixture 5 times. 

Following this procedure takes some time, but made a super silky batter!

text:
I've made this cake several times and it's always come out beautifully. 
I do like my cakes less sweet so I've cut it down to 1 cup of sugar. I've discovered a secret... for a really great textured cake is to beat the butter and sugar till almost all the granuals are gone. Then add the egg yolks as instructed and beat till all the sugar granuals have melted into the mixture. Plus add 1/4 cup of canola or my choice is grapeseed oil for a moist cake. Then add the flour/milk as instructed. I think you'll notice a huge improvement with the final result.

text:
This cake turned out great.  I just made it for my son's birthday party.  I made two versions and cooked them in a 9x13 nonstick pan lined with parchment paper.  The first batch I made my own cake flour with 2tbl cornstarch and 1/2 tsp baking powder per cup of flour (and in addition, I still added the 2 tsp baking powder the recipe calls for).  I also used buttermilk instead of milk and added 1/4 tsp baking soda to counteract acidity.  Finally I used four egg yolks and two eggs - beating the egg whites and folding them into the batter before the flour addition.  The batter was so thick I thought it was a dud but this turned out fluffy, rose nicely,was fantastic.  The second batch I again made my own cake flour and used regular milk and four eggs, beating the egg whites and adding them after the flour.  The batter was not as thick which I thought would work better but this cake turned out only OK - it didn't rise as much, was a little overdone looking.  Didn't taste bad, just wasn't as good as the first.  So to review - I would suggest using buttermilk and six egg - eight egg yolks.  For those that had dry texture - one reason could be the eggs weren't at room temp - if they are cold they will ruin your cake.

text:
This baked up into a respectable cake. It is quite yellow, as promised, because of all those yolks. However, what I learned is that there is something very positive to be said of cakes that also utilize whole eggs. That something is lightness. Although these layers were quite moist and tender as promised, the crumb was dense. I prefer a less heavy, more feathery cake. Not only is this possible, it is relatively easy to achieve. A superior recipe to this one is Yellow Clooney Cake on this website. If you try them both, I'm confident you'll agree. All in all, this is a reasonable option that won't undermine your reputation for baking prowess. It's just not, however, as close to my ideal as the recipe mentioned above.

text:
Holy . At first I was a little worried because of all the bad reviews, but I am SOOOO glad I went with my gut and tried this recipe! I followed it to the letter, and beat the hell out of the butter/sugar, and after each egg. I don't like my sifter, so I threw it out....instead I put all the dry ingredients in a bowl and wisk them over and over again, to get the air in there. It works like a charm! I got 28 cupcakes from this. I tried the batter before I baked it and it is FANTASTIC! I couldn't wait till the cupcakes were cooled off, I HAD to try one. I don't know what the previous reviewers were talking about when they said it was dry or tasted like cornbread. It was moist, and the most delicious yellow cake I have EVER had! Make sure you beat the  out of the butter/sugar/yokes, and only mix in the flour mix and milk until incorporated, starting and ending with flour. It seriously makes all the difference!

text:
Delicious - if your cake ends up dry, you're NOT doing something right.
Make sure to:
A) Cream the butter and sugar together until super fluffy.  Don't be afraid to overbeat in this phase
B) make sure NOT to overbeat cake mixture! That's how u get the weird clumpy texture on top and thats how it separates. 
C) Make sure the eggs are nice and fluffy as this helps with the cake's rise.

Use 6 egg yolks and 2 egg whites, use buttermilk.

text:
Warning- you will not be able to go back to yellow box cakes after this yellow scratch cake!! 

*** If you want moist and fluffy results, it is extremely important NOT to knock out all of the air that you have whipped in***If you add the eggs, flour, or milk all at once, it will knock most of the air out and you will end up with a dense cornbread type cake. 

For fool proof results cream the butter and sugar until light and fluffy, then add the eggs one at a time, then add the flour and milk separately a little bit at a time, 30 seconds apart from  one another while your still mixing on medium speed and you mixture will remain airy and fluffy. 

Towards the end of the baking time, you will also need to watch this cake like a hawk. It will go from undone and gooey to a clean toothpick in a matter of a minutes.

I'd also recommend making this cake one day ahead of when you plan to serve it. It tastes heavenly the next day.

Thanks David for sharing this wonderful recipe!

text:
This cake is soooo good. It's everything I was searching for. Moist, fluffy texture. Perfectly sweet, buttery flavor. I will look no further. As for the extra whites...make a meringue for a pie...try a healthy omelet, but this recipe needs no alterations. Cream the sugar and butter well. Don't over mix once you start with that flour. If you develop too much gluten, your cake will be tough. I don't even wait until all the flour is fully incorporated to start adding milk. Start and end with dry. 3 dry, 2 wet, alternating fairly quickly. Don't overbake. Bake til it's done...different ovens and other factors like elevation will affect cooking time. Thanks for this recipe.

I used this recipe as a base for a lemon cake.  I 1/2'd the recipe since I was experimenting and the cake turned out much better than what I expected.  Since I 1/2'd the recipe used 2 whole eggs and 2 egg yolks.  I should've used 3 egg yolks and 1 whole egg but none-the-less the cake was de-lish!! FYI.....egg yolks make the cake dense (heavy) while egg whites make them light and airy.  If you don't want a dense cake you will need to used use a few whole eggs in place of just egg yolks. text:
This is by far the best cake I have ever made from scratch.  I followed the recipe exactly, modifying only by adding 1 tsp of pure almond extract (I think that added quite a lot to the overall flavor).  

I split it into 3 layers (8 in. pans) and it came out wonderfully.  One thing to note:  The cake will stick, luckily I lined the bottom of the cake pans with parchment paper cutouts before baking, so I didn't have a problem.

Also, I creamed the butter and sugar together for 5+ minutes at the start and followed the directions precisely about beating in the yolks one at a time.  When you get to the flour/milk stage, make sure not to overmix.  I think this was the key, the cake was fluffy and moist, with amazing flavor.

I made the microwave lemon curd (from this site) and put a layer of that and Special Buttercream Frosting (also from this site) in between each of the layers and frosted the outside with the buttercream.  It was delicious!

I just acquired a Kitchen Aid for Christmas, with high hopes of improving my (novice) baking skills, and was excited about trying this recipe.  And oh my word, it was delicious and oh so easy! text:
I've made this recipe twice (layer cake and cupcakes) and it was an equal success both times. An easy recipe for a moist, flavorful cake that smells wonderful while baking. Just follow the directions as given. All-purpose flour will work fine, but cake flour will give a decidedly finer texture. For best results, as with any cake recipe, you'll want to be sure to the butter is room temp and that you cream the butter and sugar thoroughly for at least several minutes. After this, take care not to overbeat, especially when adding the flour and milk. Mine were done baking right at 25 minutes. It will be yellow and might APPEAR underdone, but if the cake starts to brown at all, that's too long. The instant it passes the tap-and-spring-back test, it's ready.

WOW!!!  I have been looking for a long time for a good "basic" homemade cake that is NOT heavy and dense and I've finally found it.  I did change two things based on personal cake baking experience/preference: I used half butter/half butter-flavored shortening, and I used 2 less eggs but whipped the all of the egg whites to peaks with a dash of cream of tartar, and then folded them in at the very end... LIGHT, perfect moist crumb, baked up evenly.  Popped it in the FREEZER for 15 mins to cool (TIP: this makes your cake super moist).  This time I did a nice dark chocolate cream cheese frosting, but from here on out I will forever use this recipe in place of a boxed cake mix for so many different kinds of cakes... total keeper!!!!

text:
This is so good that I've erased several sentences to find the perfect beginning to my review... I really don't know how to start other than to say that this really is the cake that birthday dreams are made of.  I have been looking, experimenting, and researching for many years to find the perfect yellow cake, and it was this simple the whole time.  This is absolutely the best cake I've ever tasted (let alone made), and that's coming from a professional baker with a healthy obsession with cake.  I'm taking the time to write this review because I feel that the recipe deserves it, and other people doing their research (as I was) might benefit from it.

If you are having trouble with this recipe, just remember that EVERYTHING matters when it comes to baking.  No substitutions or shortcuts will get you the right result.  The butter and sugar should be beaten until the mixture looks almost white and fluffier than whipped icing (this takes at least 5 minutes on medium-high speed on a stand mixer; don't worry, your patience will pay off).  The flour must be sifted, and all-purpose flour will NOT work the same as cake flour.  If care is taken to follow all instructions exactly, this cake will not disappoint!

text:
I read a ton of reviews before making this.  Here’s what I did and it DID turn out to be the BEST dang cake. We devoured this with a basic chocolate butter cream frosting. I substituted the milk with 1 cup buttermilk and changed eggs to 4 yolks and 2 whole eggs.  I took a lot of time putting the cake together creaming and creaming and creaming the sugar and butter for a while. Then I added each egg yolk at a time and still beat and cream a lot in between each one. I whisked the flour mixture awhile instead of sifting it as my sifter is too small to allow the salt through.  I baked in two 8” rounds and found it only took about 20 minutes to cook. I was careful to check that early on after others talked about being dried out.  This cake was not dry. It was moist and tasted unlike any other yellow I’ve ever had.  Amazing Cake!

text:
I finally tried this cake because I had exactly 8 leftover egg yolks in the freezer. I made it with half butter and half 80% vegetable oil margarine. It was very good. I planned to frost it with caramel frosting. After tasting a little piece I trimmed off for my hungry impatient toddler, I decided to leave it unfrosted. I don't recall ever saying nah I won't frost this one. This is a very rich, very moist cake. It's good as is. (If folks are having trouble with baking scratch cakes with recipes that seem to work for others...1.)Make sure all ingredients are room temp, including the milk. This is very important. 2.)Cream butter and sugar VERY well. I only have a hand mixer, so I know it works just fine for this. Be patient and cream well. 3.)Don't over mix after the flour and milk are added. Mix more than you would for muffins. Blend well but don't go crazy. 4.)Test your oven temperature on both sides. 5.)DON'T GIVE UP! After a half dozen scratch cakes, they'll start tasting really good. After making a dozen+ of them, they'll start tasting great.) Thanks for a great recipe!

text:
Wow!  This was my first scratch cake, and man was it a winner!  Unbelievably light and fluffy!  I used 1 whole egg and 6 yolks (because I broke the first yolk), and otherwise followed the recipe to a T.  I used cake flour, sifted the dry ingredients, used an electric mixer to completely beat in 1 yolk at a time, and alternated adding milk and flour just like it says.  The result was a thick, beautiful batter--much thicker than box batter.  I was almost concerned about it, but it rose beautifully and turned an even, light golden brown on top.  Bake time was specific to my oven--you just have to watch it.  This cake was superior in every way.  Amazing texture, excellent taste.  I will never by a boxed yellow cake again!

text:
Warning:  If you are looking for a light and fluffy yellow cake like what you get in the box, then go to your grocery store and pick up prepackaged cake mix.  That being said, this cake is good.  It's definitely a heavier and denser cake than you might expect if you are used to box cake mix.  It is still very moist though.  I made everything as written with the exception of using all-purpose flour instead.  We sifted the all-purpose flour twice and then measured the 2 c. out after so it would be nice and fine and silky like cake flour.  I made my own frosting using the Vanilla - Chocolate Powdered Sugar Frosting recipe on here (highly recommended...I did the chocolate version) This cake is good, but I don't feel like it's outstanding.  If I wanted to make a yellow cake again, I would still probably experiment with some other recipes.  I agree with the people on here who commented that it has a slight sweet cornbread flavor to it.  The texture is nothing like cornbread, but it does have a subtle hint of that taste to it.  If you are looking for a good cake that you know will turn out, I would recommend this.  If you have time to test out some other recipes to compare and contrast which is best, I wouldn't hesitate to do that though either.

text:
Great taste and SO easy to make.  You definitely have to follow directions though.  A tip for those worried about dry cake:  combine 2 cups of water and 1 cup sugar.  Bring to a boil for 3 minutes and then let cool.  Pierce your cooled cake layers with a fork and then use a spray bottle to distribute the sugar mixture.  *Note: DO NOT spray the layers too much or they will become soggy!  Just a few spritzes...you will have a lot of the sugar mixture left over.  This is a great way to add moisture to a dry cake without starting all over

text:
Thank you David!! This recipe most certainly is amazing. I did change a couple things though, not because I thought your recipe was lacking, but because I have a deep palette and love to over-indulge on flavor (lol):

- I replaced the milk with equal portions of buttermilk/half & half
- I used 1.5 Tbsp of vanilla (I'm a vanilla )
- I used unsalted butter (it seems to cream better with sugar for me), and added 1/4 tsp salt to the recipe, mixing it in with the flour (as the recipe calls for)
- I baked in a glass pyrex for probably 35-40 minutes

Not that your recipe called for this, but I did use my kitchen aid mixer.

The cake was DELICIOUS!!! Extremely moist, perfectly done, and made my entire house smell like twinkles!! I thank you tremendously for sharing this recipe with everyone, and completely concur - it's by FAR the best recipe I've tried. I cannot wait to use this as a base for my twinkie trifle, apple cinnamon swirl bundt cake, and blueberry cake! Thanks again, my friends and family will be thanking me because of you!

My favorite recipe from this site so far!

I love baking, but I normally used a cake mix for yellow cakes.  Scratch yellow cakes seem to be so easy to dry out!  This cake however was absolutely wonderful!  I followed the directions for the cake exactly and filled it with a strawberry filling and frosted it with buttercream icing. I think this is the first cake I've made from scratch that I've ever been proud of.  It comes out very dense and sweet (almost too sweet), similar to a pound cake but not quite as heavy.  As other reviewers noted, you need to really beat the sugar and butter mixture until VERY fluffy.  Also, be sure to use cake flour--all purpose will make it dry and course.   I needed a cake for strawberry shortcake so I tried this one.  I made a half batch and filled one 9 in. pan.  I topped it with sugared strawberries and whipped cream.  My husband and I couldn't stop eating it!

text:
I was hesitant because of some of the negative reviews, but this cake was totally scrumptious - moist and light textured.  I doubt if I will ever make a yellow cake from a mix again!  I made it as a birthday cake in a 13x9x2 pan with Caramel Frosting and everyone raved about it.  Like some other reviewers, I did not have a use for the leftover egg whites, so I used 4 eggs instead the 8 egg yolks.  I only had one cup of cake flour, so I used White Lily All Purpose for the rest.  I did beat the butter and sugar thoroughly and then beat each of the eggs in one at a time (they were cold from the fridge). Then I beat about 3 minutes once all the ingredients were in the mixing bowl.  I didn't sift the flour or do anything special.  So if mine came out as well as it did, I can't imagine how anyone has it come out like cornbread! I think if it comes out dry, it may be that womone is overcooking it.  I did bake at 325 instead of 350 as my oven runs a little hot, and took the cake out the second the center wasn't wiggly.  This will be my go-to yellow cake recipe from now on.  Thanks for sharing the recipe!

text:
after trying many different vanilla / plain cake recipes i was generally dissatisfied. Recently i made a batch of Swiss meringue buttercream and had 11 egg yolks left over which i refuse to waste! I searched for a recipe using only yolks not whole eggs / whites. This recipe was beautiful soft moist with a soft fluffy texture.  The only thing i would say is that it is soft which i personally love and prob would not use this to do a tiered cake or one that needs to be covered in fondant (although this suits me fine as i hate fondant)  . One adjustment for anyone who would want a more firmer structure  is to use 6 or 7 yolks and one whole egg or play around with that!

I forgot to mention that i let my kitchenaid cream the butter and sugar for a good 6/7 minutes while i prepared the other ingredients and tins as this makes a world of difference to ANY cake! Also the previous review stated that the cooking time was too long...For me the cooking time was EXACTLY 25 mins and not a second longer or shorter so be sure to Know your ovens little quirks. Mine is a standard gas oven and to gas mark 4 (in the UK)

text:
I doubled the recipe to make a cake and cupcakes--just ate one of the cupcakes, and even slightly overdone, it was moist and tender.  Loved it!  Since I used all purpose flour, I replaced 1/4c flour (per recipe) with 1/4c cornstarch to reduce the protein content in the flour.  I also used 4 whole eggs.  I've always thought yellow cakes were a pain in the neck because of all the yolks, but it worked just great with whole eggs, and tastes delicious!  This is my new go-to recipe.

text:
This turned out amazing! I did some mods however. I realized I had 6 eggs and 3 really ripe bananas. Enter the perfect marriage of eggs/bananas. I used the 3 really ripe bananas and 2 egg yolks in place of the 8 egg yolks (you can sub 1 banana for 1 egg in any recipe usually. I did this all the time when I avoided dairy, and good for those watching cholesterol). 

I just taste-tested the resulting cupcakes because of my sneaky 2 year old who swiped one from the counter before appointed birthday cupcake time for my 12yo. They are moist and amazing, and using the egg yolks with the bananas there is no dryness to fathom.  

Everything else I followed to original recipe. They taste like yellow cake meets banana bread, with not too much of either taking over. 

All ingredients used were organic (really makes a huge difference in quality, healthfulness,  and taste).

text:
I read many of its reviews before attempting this recipe and I have never been more careful to follow a recipe exactly.  It had the texture of cream when it went into the pan, so it didn't really "spread".  I overcooked it.  I set the timer for 25 minutes and after 20 minutes, I tested with a toothpick fearing that I had overcooked it.  Relieved at the gooey yellow that clug to my toothpick, I proceeded to clean up the mess from my baking, when suddenly, my timer went off.  My cakes were dark carmel color and sure enough, my toothpick was clean clean clean!  I wish someone had warned me and I want to warn the next novice baker.  You can go from gooo to clean clean clean in 5 minutes, so check again after 2 1/2.  

Even though I overcooked it, by toothpick measures, the cake tasted yummy.  So very different from Betty Crocker.  It was eggy.  I think I would try to make it with less eggs next time.  Also, it did not release nicely from the pan.  I used my calphalan non stick pans.  I buttered them and floured them - I'm new to this, so I perhaps didn't do it correctly, but when I attempted to free the cake, the bottom part of the cake was left in the pan.  

It is the fluffiest cake I have ever experienced.

text:
This cake is wonderful- fluffy, light, and delicious!

Here's what I do- make sure all ingredients are ROOM TEMPERATURE- milk, butter, eggs, etc. When you cream the butter and sugar, let the mixer cream it for at LEAST 5-10 minutes on high. After you add the flour and milk, scrape down the sides of your bowl and mix again. Also, do NOT over-beat! Just mix until combined. 
I use this to make cupcakes, and it takes roughly 15-16 minutes at 350. 

Also, a trick for moist cakes is after you turn it out, spray it with a simple syrup- mix 1/2c water with 1/2c sugar, heat till boiling, turn off the heat. Let it cool, the pour into a spray bottle. Spray it on your cake and this will help retain moisture.

If you follow the recipe EXACTLY in terms of flour type, egg yolks, etc., this recipe is fantastic!

I love this cake, its simple and just delicious! It came out spongy, soft and light. I've made this recipe a few times, each time better tasting! It got a little sticky in my cake pan so i lined it with wax paper, and it came out just perfect! You could substitute the 8 egg yolks for 4 whole eggs, unless you want the proper Yellow Cake. Usually too much baking powder hardens the cake, but 1/3 extra the amount wouldn't hurt. Also, for icing this cake you might want to crumb coat and refrigerate it first, because it can get a little crumby...and many thanks for sharing, wonderful recipe!

text:
I have made many yellow cakes though the years, but this one is the absolute best!  Fantastic!  I would give it 10 stars if I could.  Such a simple recipe, too.  I'm lactose intolerant, so subbed Earth Balance for the butter and coconut milk for the milk.  Also used 4 large eggs instead of 8 yolks.  I had a traditional yellow birthday cake with chocolate frosting just recently from a fancy local bakery and truth be told, no comparison to this cake.  From now on, it's David's Yellow Cake for all special occasions.  For those reviewers whose cakes came out dry or like cornbread, perhaps the measurement of ingredients was off, the batter was over mixed, oven was too hot, or cake baked too long.  This cake is light, fluffy, and so deliciously moist.  Doesn't even need frosting, it's THAT GOOD!  Thank you, David for a great recipe.  My family thanks you, too!

text:
This recipe is just what I have been looking for!  I have tried many yellow cake recipes, and this one came out far ahead of the rest.  I used whole eggs instead of yolks because I didn't have a use for the whites, and they don't freeze well by themselves.  The batter was so fluffy and light, I couldn't believe it!  The cake came out delicious, with a light and delicate crumb.  Perfect.  The tricks are sifting twice, creaming the butter for a long time (3-5 minutes), and mixing well after each egg or egg yolk.  It did take longer to bake than I had thought, but I had done a 1.5x recipe and was baking in a deeper pan (for shaping, I used it for a castle cake).  When it's lightly browned on top, and a toothpick in the center comes out clean, it's done.  I HIGHLY recommend an over thermometer - I have never had an oven that cooks at the exact temperature you set it too.

text:
I was a little leary about trying this cake, but it turned out great!! It was also DE-licious, thanks to all the great tips from others.  I substituted 2 tbsps. of cornstarch for 2 tbsps. of flour for each cup of flour, sifted my dry ingredients twice, used cake flour, 2 tsps. of pure vanilla extract, made sure to cream the butter and sugar well and then creamed it well again with each egg yolk added, lined my cake pans with parchment paper, and tapped the pans on the counter to rid any air bubbles prior to cooking.  It was the perfect yellow cake recipe.  Thanks David!!

text:
FINALLY! A wonderful, from SCRATCH, yellow cake.  I bumped up the servings to 18 to fill my 11x15 sheet cake pan and it was the perfect amount of batter.  The cake came out moist and fluffy and tasted perfect.  For those of you who are having difficulty, make sure you are creaming your butter and sugar long enough (5-10 min) - this used to be my problem as a newbie baker with getting my cakes nice and fluffy.  Mine used to turn out looking like "cornbread".  Also use the right type of flour, all the ingredients in baking need to be correct.  Great cake!  Thanks so much - this is my go-to yellow cake now :-)

text:
I was searching for a from scratch yellow cake recipe and decided on this one cause it had the best reviews. People seemed to like it just how it was without having to tweak it to make it work. For this reason I thought it was pretty fool proof. Maybe it was something I did wrong but I was highly disappointed. I followed the directions to a T but my cake came out looking like it had been hit by a meteor. It was high on the sides and sunken in the center. Cooked evenly but totally misshapen. I've cooked many cakes before and have never had this problem. The flavor was not great and it was very dry. Once I researched the problems I had I discovered that mabye I was disappointed because I had just chose the wrong cake recipe. I was looking for a moist cake with a fine crumb and a sweet flavor. This cake had a large dry crumb and was somewhat similar to cornbread with a tough crust. I continued my search and found just what I was looking for in the Betty Crocker recipe for yellow cake.  I gave it 2 stars becuse the problems could have partially been my fault and it wasn't a horrible tasting cake, just wasn't exactly what I was looking for. If you want a large crumb cake that will stand up to a heavy frosting this may be what you're looking for. But if you want a soft, moist, fine crumb, fool proof cake go with the Betty Crocker recipe.

text:
Just made this recipe fpr birthday cupcakes. The cupcakes are for my boyfriend's b-day tomorrow, so this was going to be a test batch...but they turned out so darn nice, (No tweeking at all) that I just decorated them and can't wait to serve them! It's a beautiful batch of cupcakes! I admit, I was a little scared by the 8 yolk requirement, but you can't argue with the sheer volume of god reviews, so I gambled. The texture was very very light and fluffy. One hour after cooling, they are very moist without being heavy. I wasn't just pleased at how light they are...I was shocked! I thought for sure they would be heavy..but NO! Hurrah! I was very careful to sift dry ingredients twice through and used "soft as silk" cake flour. I also creamed the butter and sugar for a LOOONG time...but then was careful to ONLY MIX IN FLOUR MIXTURE UNTIL INCORPORATED!!! I wonder if the technique is what stumps some new bakers? There was no trace of any corn bread texture or flavor, unlike what some reviewers have reported. The texture of my cupcakes is so light, it floats. That said, if you're an enthusiastic froster. this is a delicate cake, so be gentle. Rave!!!

text:
This is delicious.  I don’t know how anyone could give this recipe a poor review unless perhaps they missed a step.  Its really important to aerate the flour before mixing it with the other ingredients.  This recipe asks you to sift the flour in order to accomplish this.  If you skip this step and your cake doesn’t feel fluffy- well thats why.  Its also always a good idea to check your oven temperature. I also try to check the cake 3-5 minutes before the recommended cooking time just because I do think my oven tends to run a little warmer, this helps me prevent the cake from becoming dry from over baking.

I made it exactly as written.  I thought it was good! It needs to be known that box mixes for yellow or white cake will always be different. It just goes down to the science of using real ingredients. I brushed the cake with a simple syrup while it was warm to prevent dryness (just in case due to the reviews). The cake was a little dense but not abnormally for a scratch yellow/white cake.. I thought the flavor was great and I would make it again! I just think you need to expect it to be different than a box mix. Its crucial that you familiarize yourself with correct butter creaming techniques and follow the instructions well. I also folded in the ingredients by hand after beating in the eggs per my preference. Overmixing after the eggs are added can ruin a cake.

I made the recipe exactly as-is. I was careful to whisk the dry ingredients together well, and to cream the butter and sugar thoroughly, before adding the yolks slowly, one by one. I weighed the batter so I would have even layers. Since my oven seems to run a little cold, I had to bake for 28 minutes at 350 and then another 5 minutes on convection at 350. The cake was a pleasing color with a good crumb, and not to sweet. I filled and frosted it with a cocoa ermine frosting that was just right... again not too sweet, and super smooth. This combination made the best traditional "birthday cake" I've made yet. I topped it with non pareils, cut piroulines in half and stacked them around the edges.

text:
This is a great cake.  It is a bit more dense than store bought pre mix, but holds up very will to chocolate glaze.  The author provided the recipe, he did not explain proper preparation procedures.  That is not his fault.  Cream the butter and sugar correctly.  The egg yolks should be a room temp prior to inclusion. The second time I made the recipe I lowered the oven temp to 335 degrees and tested the center every 5 minutes after 30 minutes of bake time.  This eliminated the concave top. As an additional note, baking powder has a limited shelf life.  Make sure the powder you are using is fresh or the cake may not expand as expected.

text:
AMAZING! I made an account just to write a review of this cake. I read previous reviews and substituted the cake flour for  1 3/4c AP flour + 1/4c corn starch. I also took one tablespoon out of my cup of milk and replaced it with 1T of vinegar to make buttermilk. I sifted all my dry ingredients twice. Be sure to thoroughly mix your wet ingredients. Beat the yolks in one at a time, mixing for 30 seconds after each egg. Be sure to scrape down the sides after every addition. Alternate adding the milk and flour a little at a time, again, beating for 30 seconds and scraping down the sides after each addition. Be sure to start and end with adding the milk. All the beating whips a lot of air into the mix making the cake super light and fluffy. It was not dense or eggy like others complained. Take the time to do each step right and you will have an amazing cake! Save your egg whites for a Swiss Meringue buttercream frosting!

To those who did not like this recipe, cake baking is a science.  If you don't understand the science behind it, your cakes will not consistently turn out well.  Here are a few tips to getting a quality cake:

1. Make sure you preheat your oven.  If you put your cake into a cold oven, the baking powder will not have the opportunity to work properly.
2. Make sure all of your cold ingredients are at room temperature and make sure your butter is not too soft/hard.  You should be able to press your finger into the butter and have it leave an indent.
3. Sifting your dry ingredients together helps to add air into the flour and incorporate them.  I usually do this step twice.  Also, be careful if your sifter has a fine mesh.  The salt may not go through the mesh.  In that case, add the salt at the end and gently stir it into the other dry ingredients.  Also, when you measure your flour, do NOT scoop it out of the bin with your measuring cup, stir the flour in the bin and then spoon it into your measuring cup. Level the cup off without mashing down on the flour.  If you scoop, you WILL use too much flour and your cake will be dry.
4. Let's face it, if you do not have a stand mixer, your arm will get VERY tired if you cream your butter and sugar together to the proper consistency, but it can be done.  In my stand mixer, on medium-high speed, this step takes nearly 7-8 minutes to reach the proper consistency.  When properly creamed, the butter mixture will be almost white.  I suspect t

text:
Excellent recipe,but I am a baker, so here's my alterations.
Sorry David, but I'm not about to waste the egg whites , so I used 5 whole eggs.  ALWAYS,ALWAYS use room temperature eggs and butter  when making cake recipes.  Everything else was spot on.... EXCEPT>>>>>>>>>> If you want a lighter, fluffier cake, add a tablespoon and a half of dry powdered milk to the dry ingredients.    When baking, it  creates and releases air into the batter , making it lighter, fluffier.
I always prefer a triple layer to a double layer cake, so you can either add 1/3 more ingredients for the third layer, or just use the batter and distribute into 3 separate  cake pans, your choice. Use less baking time if you don't add extra ingredients for a triple layer.
If you've made the cake before, and felt it was a little dry, you can add 1/3 cup of vegetable oil to the mix before baking.

THIS. WAS. PERFECTION. If anybody says it was dry they did not bake it right or mix it right. So Moist. So perfect. I need not ever try another way of making yellow cake. Yellow cake is meant to be simple and I will leave it that way moving forward.

I used 9 in pans and cooked for about 20 mins. As it says, Add eggs one at a time starting with yolk only eggs. Good tip from net- put 2 tbs of cornstarch in cup then fill with flour and level. First successful scratch cake tho other try was 20 yrs ago :) thanks for recipe!

I made this cake for my mother's 66th birthday. I didn't want to have to eat an egg white omelette the next day or make an angel cake, so I subbed four whole eggs for the 8 yolks. text:
I have made this cake several times. My first few attempts were highly successful. I use this as the cake for my Peach Upside down  Cake.  I have unsuccessfully made this cake 3 times....And, in hindsight it was all my own fault.  over mixing can ruin this cake and it wont rise. it states clearly until just combined.....so you have to turn the mixer off and stir it. using anything but cake flower will make it too dense. not sifting your flower or creaming your butter and sugar properly will make it have the "corn bread" consistency. And, Trying to make this cake quickly will ruin it as well.  You have to take your time. You have to follow the steps on this one exactly. If you think your butter and sugar is creamed? Cream it some more. make sure each egg is  competently beaten into the batter before adding the next. It is a great cake. But, there is no wiggle room. you have to follow the directions exactly.

I make this regularly but as cupcakes. The recipe will make about 24 cupcakes when filled 2/3. I usually make it with six yolks and one whole egg though. That makes the cake a little less dense and we enjoy it that way.  I have used regular flour instead of cake flour, but it's much better with cake flour . Sometimes I change up the vanilla extract and try almond, orange, or lemon combinations. The cupcakes freeze perfectly in freezer bags. I know it sounds like I change everything, but I love to experiment and this has become our go to cupcake recipe for every family birthday, shower, etc. Everyone loves it!

I've made this recipe many times and followed it explicitly. I've always had trouble with the baking time, but it turns out well, still moist and fluffy. This time, I lacked milk and good baking powder, so I improvised with the help of Google searches and experimentation to ensure that the resulting combination reacted well and tasted fine. Instead of 3/4 quarter cup milk, I used about 2/3 plain 3% yogurt, which tasted light and sour. And I used 1/2 tsp fresh baking soda. These were added separately. For the first 30 minutes i placed it on a higher rack, then moved the cake one rack lower. I baked for a total of  45 minutes. It browned nicely all over, and the top is fluffy and golden. The middle did poof up, then it sunk a little. Tasted even better and was more most with the yogurt than with milk! 

For icing,i cooked 1/2 cup of the yogurt and 1 cup granulated white sugar until smooth and a little bit more viscous. I added more sugar because it was not sweet enough. text:
Never fails. Have made this recipe many times and it's always delicious. If you like boxed cakes - you will probably not like this. It's different (IMO much better)but if you have only made boxed cakes this will be really different. I always have my eggs and butter room temp before baking this. Have made it as a sheet cake, as a double layer, and as a triple layer cake (just adjusting the times). If I make it as a layer cake I make a simple chocolate truffle filling for in between layers then a chocolate ganache for the outside but it's delicious as is without any frosting or filling. My daughter likes orange in her cakes so I mix in a bit of orange zest if I'm making it for her. I have also made it with 3 egg yolks and 2 whole eggs (when I didn't have enough eggs) and that worked out ok too. I prefer the original recipe but sometimes have to improvise. The recipe is solid and reliable as is :) Thanks for sharing!

text:
I followed this recipe exactly, and it baked up very moist, tender, and sweet. I usually do not enjoy yellow cake, because it is so often dry, but this was very tender and delicious.

One of the other posters was correct - this cake does have an eggy, almost custard-like taste while it's warm, but that egg taste does dissipate once it's cooled. I was a bit concerned when I tasted the toothpick I had used to test the center. It tasted like a custard to me. But I had read that the egg flavor goes away, and so it did. You do not need to adjust the amount of egg yolks, because that is what gives it that yellow color and tender crumb. Don't over bake it, let it cool completely, and that custard flavor will mellow.

It is important to periodically test with a toothpick; the spring test is not reliable. There should be moist crumbs clinging to the toothpick. If it comes out wet, give it a few more minutes and test again. If it comes out perfectly clean, it is overdone and will be dry. If there are still moist crumbs clinging, it's perfect. 

One more thing is that I would recommend adding a circle of parchment paper, greased and floured, to the bottom of the pan to encourage quick release. It is VERY important to grease and flour the pan, and a good idea to add that parchment circle, as the cake is so tender that it will fall apart if it sticks.

text:
Delicious! This cake was super easy to make and tastes great. I had no problem with texture or flavor. The 8 egg yolks worried me, but I followed the recipe exactly as written and was not disappointed. As others have stated, make sure you really cream the butter/sugar together (and it goes without saying, use REAL butter). Eggs/butter should be brought down to room temp naturally for best results (I throw them on the counter a couple of hours before I start baking). I used a hand-mixer for butter/sugar, then to add in the eggs/vanilla. Once it's super creamy, I then added the flour and milk (alternating, starting/ending with flour) and mixed it in by hand -  not beaters. Don't overcook the cake (stab with fork, if a few crumbs come off on the fork, it's ready - if it comes out clean, probably overcooked, cook it less next time). This is going to be my go-to yellow cake from now on for sure! I love this cake.

text:
I followed this recipe exactly.  I just used two 9" cake pans instead of 8".  I made sure that all of the cold ingredients were room temp before mixing.  Another thing that I did was I cut an old towel into strips (the width of my cake pans), wet the strips in cold water, then wrapped the strips around the outside of my pans before baking (I use large safety pins to keep strips in place).  I learned this from a woman who worked as a professional baker for several decades.  This helps the cake bake evenly so you don't have burned edges and raw middles.  It also keeps the cake level as it bakes.  The cake was very good!  It was not dry or dense and tasted 1000% better than any box mix!  I've seen yellow cake recipes with an extensive list of ingredients but this recipe is good just the way it is.  Thank you for sharing it!

The best yellow cake ever. I watched the video and it was helpful. Cake flour gives this cake a fluffy, perfect texture.
 -Iced our cake with Homemade Caramel Icing. 1/2 cup unsalted butter, 1 Cup packed Dark Brown sugar, 1/4 cup milk, Pinch of Kosher Salt, 1/4 tsp. Vanilla Extract, 2 cups sifted Powdered Sugar.
-Melt butter in double boiler, gradually whisk in brown sugar until sugar is melted, add milk, salt, vanilla, whisking occasionally, bring to slow boil, remove from heat, cool in large mixing bowl ,gradually whisk in powdered sugar

I'm disappointed in how my cupcakes turned out and won't use this recipe again, although I am happy to hear others enjoyed it nonetheless.

text:
This is the best yellow cake I have ever eaten.  I went on line and looked up yellow cake and this site popped up. I baked the cake, making only one change 1. I added 1/4 cup cultured buttermilk blend powder to the cake flour, this gives it a little tang. Wow!! You know how you get the crunch around the cake and the even rise and fluffy texture, well I had that. Also, when you make your icing, browning the butter will take your icing to another level. I always brown the butter because this gives way more butter/nutty flavor.  All you have to do is melt the butter in a pan until it becomes fragrant and is starting to turn A LITTLE brown (the butter smell sort of bursts through and that will tell you when to stop), take it off the heat and put it in a glass container and let it come down to room temp.

text:
I searched and searched for a light and moist (and simple) yellow cake recipe, nothing was ever good enough (and I'm not a fan of box cakes). Well as others have also said, the search ends here. This IS the ultimate yellow cake recipe, and it goes well with just about anything - with or without any toppings. I've made cupcakes, tiered cakes and custom shaped cakes out of this recipe and its just perfect for anything.  
One thing you have to be careful with is handling it - it's very very soft and breaks easily. It carved fine when I carved it into a shape, but it's very delicate to handle. Tastes awesome though, and it's worth the extra 'hassle'
I usually top it with ganache or whipped ganache, it tastes wonderful. In fact I'm going to make some right now

For those of you having trouble with the recipe - as others have suggested, make sure your ingredients are room temp, and try to follow every step exactly as written, and also.. If you own a kitchen scale, go the extra mile and weigh all the ingredients - it's worth the extra step. 

Great recipe, one worth carving into stone

I am sending this review only for those who live at high altitude!!

I tried this recipe, and followed directions WORD FOR WORD, but it did not turn out.  I don't fault the recipe for this, but for the fact that I live at 6500'.  In looking back over the recipe, I think there is a ratio of too many egg yolks and butter for high altitude.  I did add a little more flour (as is customary for HA) but after 30 minutes of baking, it was over-done on the outside, and still liquid-raw on the inside.

What DID over cook, however, tasted really good!  I love the flavor of this cake; I only wish I had tried it when I lived at 1500' !!!

text:
Fantastic recipe. I followed every direction faithfully and carefully, and ended up with two wonderful layers of yellow cake - very tasty! I managed to forget to add the milk to the batter at first, so I only added it at the end, but it hardly made any difference (of course, next time I'll try to make it right). The tops of the layers came out just a tad bit burnt, but this might be my old oven's fault. Either way, the taste and texture of the cake were perfect.

I made this cake for my sister's birthday party, and as I'm not yet that good at cake decoration, I was afraid her thirteen-year-old friends weren't going to like it so much. Nevertheless, all I got were comments about how amazing the cake was - they ate up almost all of it in under two hours!

Very impressed. I know that next time I'm certainly going to make more of the batter, since my layers seemed a little too thin.

I was looking for a good cupcake recipe and after trying a few different ones this was definitely the best. I tried the original recipe first and although it was moist and had a decent flavor I felt it could use more so I add a packet of vanilla pudding (unmade) and sifted it with the flour, baking powder, and salt. I found my batter to be a little too thin and they didn't rise properly so I added more flour till it looked thick enough about 1/4 cup. After making these minor adjustments these turned out to be great cupcakes with great flavor. They tasted so good my family ate several before I had time to frost them.

I followed the directions exactly and the only change I made was to use regular flour & cornstarch instead of cake flour. It took me quite a while to separate the eggs (one at a time), add, beat, then repeat. My problem was that I couldn't figure out when it was done-I know a bunch of people commented on that. I found the cake to be a bit dense...I did use whole milk (because I only drink whole milk)-I wonder if that just made it too thick? text:
Bottom Line, if it's bad....you messed it up somehow or are WAY to used to Box cake. I am a pretty experienced baker, I made this recipe almost exactly the way it's written ,(i added 3 tablespoons of sour cream)  and it's delicious. It tastes like a butter cake, a very rich, buttery, golden, southern cake. Its spongy in texture, fluffy, and just dense enough. I made some of the batter in to cupcakes, it's great for that too, but denser than some people might like (it also sunk in a little bit, ill have to work on fixing that when i make this into cupcakes). With a rich creamy chocolate frosting, it would rival NYC's Magnolia Bakery. I cater cakes/cupcakes, and will use this recipe again and again. I can't wait to use it as a base, and make it my own! THANK you for a perfect yellow cake...finally !! 
my boyfriend....asks to have this made for his birthday every year. he LOVED it.

this came out amazing.  i used 3 whole eggs and 2 yolks.  i also used all-purpose flour because i didn't have cake flour handy.... but i took out 2 tablespoons per cup of flour and added 2 tablespoons per cup of flour of corn starch (google helped me find out the conversion of all purpose flour to cake flour).... i think i over mixed JUST a bit and will hold back next time.... also, if this is your first time making a cake batter from scratch - this will not look like cake batter from a box... it also won't pour/spread like cake batter from a box... it's much thicker and you sort of have to spread it evenly in the cake pans yourself.  great recipe - i'll definitely make again!  thank you for sharing!

text:
I baked this cake for my boyfriend's birthday on the weekend and it was a hit! People thought it was a boxed cake mix cake but I had to let them all know that, No- it's from scratch! I frosted it with a coconut cream cheese frosting and it was delicious. I think that the cake one its own was quite sweet and I may cut down the sugar next time by 1/4C-1/2C. Also, if using frosting, it just adds to the sweetness. I followed the recommendations by naples34102 and because I didn't have cake flour, I substituted 2 tbsp cornstarch for 2 tbsp of the all purpose flour. I also used 2-9 inch pans and baked them about 23 minutes but found that the layers weren't nice and thick like a store bought cake, so I may try and double the recipe in the future to make a really tall cake. The cake itself was a hit and I am glad to have found a great basic cake recipe that is flexible to use for many kinds of cakes and different occassions without having to use a boxed mix. I just don't like articificial ingredients. Also, I am curious if anybody has attempted to make this cake healthier (for example use whole wheat flour and a more natural sugar). Please post a review if you do. Thanks for the great recipe!

text:
This cake recipe was a little more on the difficult side. I made a few changes to make it easier, and I advise you do the same, because it really works! - I used 4 whole eggs instead of 8 egg whites, and I used powdered sugar to make the sugar and butter become fluffier. If you are like me, and want to make this healthier, you can use a butter substitute instead of the real thing. I used I CAN'T BELIEVE IT'S NOT BUTTER baking sticks. It works the same as other butters, just a bit better for you. In my opinion, this was extremely tasty, but just a little hard to make. But, with my changes, hopefully your turnout will be as easy as it was for me!

text:
I made this cake using Splenda sugar substitute, because my dad's diabetic. (I had to add 3/4 cup nonfat dry milk and 3/4 tsp baking powder so it would rise properly using the substitute.)  Also, since I only had all purpose flour, I used that but substituted 2 tsp of cornmeal per cup as others had suggested.  So with that in mind, the texture is nice and "heavy" compared to boxed cake, which I'm used to.  This wasn't overly sweet, which I appreciate because very sweet cakes don't appeal to my family.  My only gripe is that it is very eggy--I've made this 3x and next time I'll try using just 4 yolks like others have.  Some people said this tastes like cornbread, and I can see the comparison because of the texture and the eggy-ness.  I read the reviews beforehand but was still surprised that it reminded me of cornbread.  No, there's not cornmeal in it but I liken it to the simple texture experiment where apples and onions are texturally indistinguishable among people who cannot smell/have their noses plugged. The textures were similar, maybe its because of the all purpose flour. The only time I made this using real sugar was when I used it for the Mandarin Orange Cake from this site, which normally uses boxed cake mix.

text:
I made a ton of substitutions out of necessity and this still came out pretty darn good.  I was out of butter, white sugar, and cake flour, and short on eggs.  I substituted shortening and sour cream for the butter - about 1/2 c each. I substituted Maui Raw Sugar for white sugar 1:1. I substituted 1 c all purpose flour and 1 c buttermilk pancake mix for the cake flour. I added the four whole eggs like someone else did instead of the 8 yolks (I don't like saving whites or yolks anyway). I doubled the amount of salt. Followed instructions as given.   The result was a surprisingly good tasting (but not so much smelling) cake. It is moist, but a tad oily for me which I attribute to the shortening.  It was a little egg-y for me also. It was light and fluffy and honestly looked just like the picture on here.  I will be trying this recipe again when I have all the ingredients on hand. 8 yolks does seem a bit much for me though; I will probably keep it to four whole eggs.

text:
This is a very good yellow cake recipe...but I had some problems with it. They were probably my own fault, so I'm going to give this recipe 5 stars anyways, because, in spite of my problems, it was an awesome cake! I was making LovestoHost's Cookie Dough Cupcakes with my sister, and she didn't want to use cake mix, so we decided to make this cake instead. The batter worked out very well, and it seemed to be a good substitute for the cake mix. However, my oven overheats, and the cupcakes (and cake) got a bit overbaked on the edge before the middle was done. Straight from the oven, the cake (even overbaked!) was as tender as could be, but as it sat, the edges got very crispy. I was disappointed, but the  finished cupcakes actually were quite moist, in spite of the edges. Altogether, I would probably make this cake again. Thanks for sharing the recipe!

text:
This is the kind of butter cake recipes I have been looking for.  I'm not big on frostings so something that's good without it is for me. This is a WONDERFUL recipe!  Took the advice of other posters and used flour with cornstarch since cake flour is a luxury this kitchen may never see.  Also only used for extra large eggs and I do insist on butter.  Another point to remember is the size of the eggs.   The second time I made this with just "large" eggs and an oblong pan.  Came out heavy and flat.  It turned out the best with 4 extra large eggs and the smaller cake pans.  A lesson learned for me!  Can't stop eating it.  Hooray for David!

text:
this cake is simply one of the moistest, most flavorful yellow cakes i've had in a long time.  i did make 2 changes, though, to suit my tastes--i used 4 whole eggs because i don't have a use for 8 egg whites and i used 3 tsp of vanilla because i'm a vanilla addict.  i made a cornstarch pudding to go inbetween the layers with ripe sliced banana, and frosted with seafoam frosting.  i did not think the recipe was too greasy, though my mother ALWAYS cuts back 25% on the fat in baking without any noticeable difference.  i also used parchment paper, so taking it out of the pans was simple.  some ovens run hotter than others, and i'm wondering if that's why some people came out with dry cakes . . . i usually set my clock for 5 minutes earlier than the lowest time, just to be sure i catch the cake at the right moment.  man i wrote a lot . . . but all because this cake deserves it!  woo hoo! go yellow cake of moistness! rock on!  ;)

text:
This recipe is SO great! However, if you are an inexperienced baker or don't follow directions EXACTLY, it has the potential to come out tough and dry. The biggest 'pitfalls' I can see are not properly creaming the butter and sugar (until it is white, smooth, and fluffy), using regular flour instead of cake flour (cake flour is necessary for texture), and not beating eggs one  a time/ stirring in other ingredients (also affect texture). Unfortunately, I learned how important these things are from experience (yikes) and hopefully I can save someone else from making the same mistakes!

I sifted the flour mixture twice - otherwise followed the recipe (I weighed the ingredients making the conversion into grams based on the info on the packaging as needed). I used King Arthur Cake Flour & "store brand" everything else. Baked on convection for 27 minutes. Lovely buttery/vanilla flavor. I made this for someone who doesn't like the "overly sweet" flavor of boxed cake mix & pre-made frosting. It was perfect for them. Texture between moist & dry - just right. I used the Special Buttercream Frosting recipe; paired nicely with the flavor of the cake.

text:
Please note that if you use all purpose flour for any cake, it isn’t going to turn out as soft and fluffy as it should. Cake flour is very different, so make sure you pay attention to that crucial detail here. There are a few bad reviews on here that I can just tell are based on this single mistake. If your cake turned out like corn bread, or too hard and chewy, AP flour is to blame. It’s supposed to be light and fluffy like air.

I’ve tried this recipe several times and will keep using it as the base for all of my yellow cakes. I did find it a little dry, and a bit bland as other reviewers have said. But the recipe is solid. You just have to use your imagination. I have added a variety of flavors to this batter, including hazelnut. I have also added 1 cup finely ground almonds. I did not need to alter the other ingredients, but I did try this recipe with 2 Tbs more butter and 2 additional eggs and it made a firmer cake when added to the almond variation. But it is not really necessary. I have also tried this recipe with slight variations in sugar. I added a few extra spoons, and found that it helped the flavor. I have used this batter for a wedding cake, but I added more yolks and slightly more cake flour to stiffen it up, it is a very soft cake in its original form and doesn’t layer well past a couple layers. Play around with it. Still my go-to yellow cake recipe, just needs a few tweaks to get it to do what you want. And stay away from the AP flour. If that’s all you have,

text:
Love this recipe. I followed the ingredients and instructions to a T. I was able to get 16 cupcakes from this recipe. I creamed the butter and sugar for about 5 minutes and sifted the dry ingredients twice as another reviewer suggested. This I think added to the light yet spongy texture. Not eggy tasting at all as some had mentioned. I did take these out of the oven at about 21 minutes in. Toothpick came out clean and they were done...I think my oven runs a bit hot. Let them cool in the fridge to seal in the moisture. A trick I do with all my cakes. This recipe will be my new “go to” for a yellow cake.

text:
I love this recipe. By the way, if your cake tastes "eggy" thats because your not using fresh eggs. All eggs from the store are washed with a chemical solution, some of which leeches through the shell and starts rotting the egg. The solution reaches a point of partially sterilizing the egg also. Backyard eggs are the way to go.

This is a wonderful recipe! I made it for my sons birthday and everyone really enjoyed it. I read though the reviews before making this cake and after making it all I can say is I  didn't have any problems at all. For those that have had issues I would ask you these questions: Did you check to see if your baking powder and cake flour were fresh? Did you "cream" the butter and sugar until is was pale and fluffy? Did you use real butter not substituting margarine? Did you use good quality vanilla extract instead of the less expensive artificial vanilla. This is a good cake but sometimes when you bake you do have to ask yourself what did I get wrong.

text:
Updated to add — forgot I made it once and now just made it again. And, for the second time, one of the two layers fell. I’m so puzzled about that, but also wanted to address some of the comments from the negative reviews. I think the only truly problematic thing with this recipe is the baking time. It took a good ten minutes more than the specified time, and note you should leave it be until it’s nicely golden brown. Make sure you cream the butter and sugar thoroughly, I let them go to town in my stand mixer bowl while I sifted/measured the dry ingredients and cracked the eggs. Also I’m going to use 50% more vanilla next time, and 1/4 cup more sugar. May try part brown sugar. And final note for everyone who says it’s like cornbread: you need a new cornbread recipe! Happy baking. Orig review — First, a note. In all my 30+ years of baking (geeezz, typing that made me feel old!), I’ve never had a cake “fall,” and this one did, at least one layer did, a little bit. Anyone have thoughts or tips on that? I’m guessing it’s something I did wrong. However, I don’t even care. This is a FABULOUS recipe! I’ve hunted and pecked for a great scratch yellow cake recipe, and now I’ll be deleting all the others from my collection. I substituted Bailey’s for half the milk, just because I felt like it, and the flavor was truly WOW-worthy. I am praying for the willpower to leave it alone until I can get it filled and frosted. text:
This will be the only recipe I will use for yellow cake. It was perfection. The keys to success are: allow butter, milk, and eggs to come to room temperature before combining; combine flour/milk in this manner--1/3 flour, 1/2 milk, 1/3 flour, 1/2 milk, 1/3 flour; and, most importantly, do not overbake--pull out at 30 minutes and no later. Absolutely delicious. I frosted the cake with 7-minute icing. Divine!

city:

country:
None
text:
Siding with those whom admonish to follow the instructions, I must say it’s crucial. The density problem is solved by whipping the butter and sugar for about five minutes. The butter should have nearly doubled in volume; appearing airy.  Another tip: use “coolish” butter, not too warm. The mixing process will warm the butter. So it’s best to start with cool butter.  Also, do not over mix the batter. Many think mixing the batter “thoroughly” will make the cake better. I know! It’s counter-initiative: once you added the ingredients as prescribed - only mix the batter until its ingredients are “just” incorporated and then stop mixing!!  Over mixing will toughen the proteins in the eggs and in the flour. Also, let the batter “rest” for about 5-10 minutes before baking it.  Lastly, do not over bake it.  Knock off 5-7 minutes of baking time. Check it!  Some ovens run hotter than others. Use the center rack. Buy an oven thermometer. All of these tricks will insure a good product.  It’s not that you can’t “follow the recipe”.  There are learned techniques that are not include in most recipes. Good luck!!

text:
Okay I figured out why people either LOVE this cake or don't like it at all. Its ratios of egg yolk/sugar/butter/flour are similar to pound cake and make it come out tasting more like pound cake than the yellow birthday cake made with oil and only a few whole eggs most people expect. It's delicious for sure, but some might find too dense. I used the modifications some suggested. I substituted 2 Tbs of flour for cornstarch since I only had all-purpose flour on hand, and used an additional 1/2 cup of the flour as well.  Also I only added 2 yolks and 3 whole eggs (one at a time) with 1/2 cup buttermilk in addition to the 3/4 cup of milk the recipe calls for. I used a cream cheese buttercream frosting and people loved the cake but it still reminded me of pound cake even with the modifications. I also waited until the butter and eggs were at room temperature. Make sure not to overbake. Mine took exactly 30 minutes.

text:
This cake was great! I've made it 3 times now (4th is in the oven). The first and second times I made it it came out absolutely perfect. I followed the directions exactly as written (except I had to make my own cake flour so I did that while the butter and sugar creamed).

The third time I made it I only had 7 eggs on hand and didn't feel like running to the store so I did 6 egg yolks and 1 whole egg. The cake was a huge hit and everyone said they liked it better than the original recipe! The other thing I did differently was 2tsp of vanilla instead of 1.5tsp. I definitely recommend this recipe to anyone looking for a good yellow cake that is light, fluffy, flavorful, and tastes great whether you like to eat it plain or frost it!

text:
I think I first tried making a yellow cake about 30 years ago. Fail. Every few years, I'd try a new recipe. Fail. So yellow cake was the one cake I never made. This one was moist  and super fluffy, neither too dense nor too airy. You really have to make sure the butter and sugar are creamed - volume should be nearly double and color should be almost white. I mixed in a Kitchenaid stand mixer at speed 6 for 5-6 mins. I did find the cake to be too sweet though. I used a 9x13 pan and  tapped the cake - gently, I thought - to check doneness after 25 mins because it seemed to be browning, and it deflated a bit where I tapped it. Next time, I'll go with the toothpick test.  I'm just excited that there will be a next time!

text:
Like all of the negative reviews say this leans more toward a cornbread than a cake. The texture is very dry and crumbly and the taste is ok. I saw the positive reviews saying that this is how cake from scratch is supposed to be and box cake is only moist because of the chemicals and additives. WRONG! And honestly should tell you right there not to use this recipe because even the most positive review says it's dry and crumbly. It is not the inherent texture of from scratch cake. Just the sheer amount of egg yolks required shows that even David knew this was a dry cake, which is why he tries to compensate with a ridiculous amount of fat to try and get it more moist, but unfortunately in the end it does not give you that moist deliciousness that makes a cake a cake.

text:
I have made this cake three times.  I have made it for birthdays every time, and everyone goes nuts for it.  I am not sure what to tell the negative reviewers.  When you bake, your butter and milk should be at room temp.  It is really critical to cream the butter and sugar together until it is really smooth.  This may take a lot longer than what is in the recipe depending on your mixer and the temperature of your butter.   I would imagine it is also critical to use baking powder and not baking soda for those who said it was flat.  For those that complained of a cornbread consistency, you may have overmixed it after you were adding the flour and milk.  You almost can't overmix it when you are creaming the butter and sugar, but when you add the flour and milk, you may want to do that part by hand and only mix until just combined as it states in the recipe.  If you use all of the correct ingredients, follow the instructions, don't overmix it and bake at the correct temperature you should be rewarded with the most amazing yellow cake you have ever tasted.

text:
I have made this cake three times now, trying to get a perfect cake.  I read through many reviews and tried some peoples' advice, and my third try gave me a great cake!  For my first cake, I followed the initial recipe to a T.  I agree with several other people that it was dry.  It turned out dry and dense.  Cake #2 was better, I took someone's advice and did buttermilk.  In cake #2 I used an extra teaspoon of baking powder, 3 whole eggs and 5 yolks, and a cup of buttermilk.  Better, but still a bit dry and dense.  My husband raved about cake #3 and said he liked it better than our wedding cake! My changes were: 9 egg yolks, 3 1/4 tsp baking powder and a little over 1 1/4 c buttermilk.  Turned out moist and not dense! Only problem was it stuck to the pan trying to get it out.  Maybe I didn't spray it well enough.

text:
Loved it! Cake came together really well, and tasted delicious. I only had AP flour, so I took out 2 tb flour and subbed in 2 tb cornstarch. Make sure to double sift the flour. Also, remember to start and end with the flour when adding to the mixture (flour in thirds, milk in half). When creaming the butter and sugar, use the whisk attachment, and whip the butter until very, very fluffy (around 5 min).

Lastly, tap the pans a couple times before putting in the oven to remove air bubbles and ensure even baking. This cake also bakes in a shorter amount of time, and to a lighter color than you think. Keep an eye on it!

I made a nice cream cheese frosting, and filled the cake with plenty of raspberries and blueberries. Yum!

text:
Wonderful recipe! I used this to make cupcakes for a birthday last minute at 3am. In my tired state, I forgot to add the baking powder and only realized once I'd spooned all the batter in the cupcake liners. So I spooned the batter out of the liners and back into the bowl, mixed in the baking powder, re-filled with new liners, and popped them in the oven convinced they would turn out terrible due to overmixing. 

Even despite my mistake, they came out great! Moist, tender, and surprisingly light+ fluffy. Good flavour too, despite my skepticism over the number of yolks and the small amount of vanilla. The only change I made was adding a scant 1/4 cup of canola oil. Perhaps this extra addition of fat is what prevented the cornbread-like texture some other reviewers are complaining about. Though I'm unsure if the oil only worked because the batter was baked into cupcakes-- it may cause a large cake to sink.

text:
Made this today and it came out wonderfully. For those of you  not as successful here are some thoughts. Don't over-cream your butter, and sugar. Butter should be at about 42-44 degrees to start. Cream butter for about 60 seconds, then slowly add sugar. Mix on medium for 2-3 minutes. When adding the dry ingredients don't over mix. Just enough so you don't see signs of flour in the batter. Finish by folding the batter together with a spatula. Don't over bake, and it should come out fine.

userID:
16386745
Display Name:
NolaMomChef
isPro:
False
followersCount:
0
followingCount:
0
madeRecipesCount:
40
favoritesCount:
116
recipesCount:
