photo:
https://images.media-allrecipes.com/userphotos/50x50/5674145.jpg
city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
Each time I make a cake, I learn a new (painful) lesson. This cake is not cornbread!!! However I think I pinpointed what is going on with this yellow cake recipe. My cake outcome was a very, very pale yellow extremely fine-textured somewhat moist cake.  It was closer to a typical wedding cake texture than a moist, more robust sponge-y cake.  My husband accurately compared the outcome to an Angel Food cake. Not over baked and I used 2 whole eggs and 4 yolks. I also used a blend of whole milk and homemade milk kefir (like buttermilk). The cake's texture has everything to do with FLOUR!!!! 
If you like a really moist sponge-y cake with larger air bubbles then DO NOT USE CAKE FLOUR. USE ALL PURPOSE flour! I spent a couple hours last night learning about affect of different flours on cake texture. BOTTOM LINE: Cake flour yields the most fluffy, tallest and driest crumbly cake. It will make the finest and driest texture (hello 4 stars).  ALL-PURPOSE will not rise as quite as tall, but it will have nice airy bubbles and it will be more MOIST.  Don't know if I will get a sponge-y yellow cake using AP but I might try this recipe again with that switch. 
FYI: All cake flour (except for unbleached King Arthur cake flour) is bleached using nasty chemicals that some tastebuds may detect as a subtle chlorine-flavor to the cake....mmmm yummy.  
TIP: You can make cake flour: Just substitute 2 Tbsp cornstarch or potato starch for each cup (16 tbsp) of unbleached AP flour.

I have been looking and looking and looking for a good scratch butter cake recipe.  This is it!  I made a few minor changes.  Instead of 8 yolks, I used 4 yolks and 2 whole eggs.  I also added a tbsp of vinegar to the milk.  This cake has a beautiful moist crumb, and rises so evenly.  For those that had trouble with texture, make sure you cream the butter well and mix throughly with the addition of the eggs.  Also be sure your eggs and milk are room temp, never bake cakes with cold eggs/milk!

I had 8 yolks left over from Swiss meringue buttercream and just had to try this recipe. I baked it into 24 cupcakes at 375 for about 18 minutes. They started to sink a bit when I took them out of the oven, so I was worried they would be a mess. However, they turned out to hold up fine. The main point is, this is THE BEST vanilla/yellow cake I've ever tasted. It's so moist that it kicks cake mix out of the ballgame. The taste is truly buttery, yellow cake.

I'm sorry, but I'm sticking with the one in the box since the taste is so similar to me can't tell the difference all too much but I still had fun making it and everyone enjoyed it so it was not a waste of time.

text:
I joined Allrecipes just to rate this.  Best cake ever!  Before this, I had yet to find a cake that could compare to the moistness of box mix, and the ones that did were too eggy or not sweet enough.  This cake was flavorful, moist and amazing.  My husband, who is not a huge dessert fan, even raved about it.  I may never use cake mix again!  Just a caveat: the batter was much thicker than I expected, so much so I had to spread it out in the pan (and I only had 9-inch pans, so it didn't even go all the way to the edge), and I baked at 300 for closer to 45 minutes for a flatter cake…and it still turned out delicious and moist!  This really is a fantastic cake recipe and hard to screw up as long as you follow the instructions!

text:
I was apprehensive about this recipe, considering the astronomical differences in some of the reviews, but it turned out quite well! I think a lot of the inconsistencies in the way the recipe turns out depends on how you combine the ingredients. Unlike other cake recipes, this one doesn't specify which method to blend everything together! 

If you use a mixer to make the cake, it should incorporate enough air to get a super fluffy cake, more like that of a boxed mix. I combined everything by hand (no access to a mixer), and while the flavor was delicious, it was a bit more dense than I expected (more like a cross between a pound cake and a sponge cake). I haven't made a lot of cakes in my day, but this seems like the most obvious reason people might be having trouble (aside from weird oven temps or changing/bad ingredients).

All that aside, the flavor of this cake was delicious! Both the batter and the finished product had a nice, sweet vanilla taste without being overwhelming. I made a double layer cake, and added blackcurrant jam between the top and bottom layers, then topped the cake with dark chocolate ganache. It was a huge hit! My boyfriend, who hates yellow cake, even admitted it was the best one he's ever had!

text:
I really hope that it is not a case of beginners luck but this cake turned out really good for me.  I had recently made 3 sugary "cornbread" cakes prior to trying this recipe which all ended up in the trash.  I was hesitant to try this recipe because of the 8 egg yolks which I felt was a bit much to waste if it didn't turn out right.  Even thought others mentioned using 4 whole eggs, I didn't want to alter the recipe. I followed the advice of many reviewers and sifted the cake flour baking power and salt twice, I beat the butter/sugar mixture for about 10 minutes, added each egg yolk one at a time and mixed it a little extra after adding the last egg. It actually turned out great.  I am thankful to the reviewer that indicated it is not a good idea to wait for the cake to turn brown.  It was done when it was a golden yellow color and I would have likely waited too long to test it without that advice.  I am going to try it again to make cupcakes for my kids birthday party next week and hope to get the same results.

text:
I generally always prefer a cake from scratch over a box mix, but not in this case.  This recipe came out eggy tasting, hard and kind of crunchy on the edges and not very pretty at all.  The only change I made was to use all purpose flour instead of cake flour, but I sifted it 3 times before using.  I would have given it just 2 stars, but the texture was light and fluffy (be sure to cream the butter & sugar for a long time if you want to use this recipe) but that's the only good thing. I can say about this recipe  I will frost with a caramel frosting to help make up for the eggy taste.  Using whole eggs may make the cake taste less like cornbread.  I thought I would never say this, but if you want a yellow cake...buy a butter recipe box mix instead of using this recipe!

This is a great and simple recipe.  I followed the recipe exactly, but I had to sub in AP for cake flour.  For every cup of AP, I took away 2tbs of flour and added 2tbs of corn starch.  I would have preferred cake flour, but didn't have any on hand.  I also used a whisk to slowly stir in the flour/milk towards the end.  Overall, this is a perfect recipe.  It's the right amount of sugar, it is moist, and it's the right consistency for a cake.  Not at all like a box cake, with which I am very familiar.  Thanks, David!

text:
I had to make a couple of minor changes due to what I had on hand (AP flour vs. cake flour and 4 egg yolks and 2 whole eggs vs. 8 egg yolks), but otherwise followed the recipe exactly. I sort of goofed on the baking though (blonde moment-hope nobody gets offended! lol). The recipe's baking time is for 2 layer cake, I was using sheet cake and didn't know exact baking time for it so I set timer for 30 minutes and was going to just check it in 5 minute intervals, which I did. After 65 minutes I knew something wasn't right because it was still "jiggly" in the center and wet looking and I've never had a yellow cake take that long! I suddenly realized the oven no longer felt very hot. I looked at the control panel and suddenly realized I had turned the oven off at some point, most likely when the 30 minute timer went off! (Boy did I feel stupid-first time I ever pulled that one.) Anyway, I turned the oven back on, left the cake in the oven throughout the preheat (or reheat in this case) and 10 more minutes later it was done. After it had cooled I made a chocolate frosting recipe I found on this site. Bottom line-even after my screw-up with the oven, though it was initially a little dry, after about 24 hours it had moistened up a bit, and overall it was awesome! I bet it would have been even better with proper baking! Great recipe, no more box cakes for me except if absolutely necessary. Thanks!

text:
This recipe certainly lived up to its ratings in my kitchen! I just made this for a friend with severe food allergies, so I substituted Earth Balance Soy Free Buttery Spread for the butter and rice milk for the milk.  After reading other comments, I brought all ingredients to room temperature.  I also chose to weigh the cake flour (224 grams) and hand mix the dry ingredients in a bowl instead of sifting.  The only problem I had was that the cake stuck in the pans and almost didn't come out.  Next time I will cut wax paper or parchment paper to line the pans.  I'm sure I'll be making this for my friend again soon!

Lot of mixed reviews had me worried but it came out wonderful. It seemed like a huge amount of egg yolks, I thought it might make the cake oily. Not dry or "cornmeal" like as others said. Always mix as little as possible! And what to do with all those left over egg whites?? Well I made meringue cookies!

text:
Perfect yellow cake recipe! Tasted like a cake from a REAL bakery (not one of those grocery store fakeries). Moist, perfect density, not crumbly at all, easy to carve (I baked 2 9" rounds for a teddy bear cake, used one for the head, the other to carve out ears). Everyone at my daughter's 1st birthday party raved about it—every plate was clean to the last crumb.

I made one ingredient change: only had 6 eggs, so I did 2 whole eggs + 4 yolks. Also didn't bother to sift the dry ingredients together, instead mixed baking powder and salt in with the butter/sugar/eggs before alternately mixing in flour and milk. I don't like to do extra dishes.

Used the left over egg whites to make "Authentic French Meringues" from this website (also delish).

Thank you David!

country:

text:
It's just my husband and I in our house so I scaled this down to make about 4 cupcakes :) I combined/followed a few other reviews' tips and they were AMAZING! I've never been able to find a great yellow cake recipe. I'm a great cook and baker, but they turn out either too dense or not enough flavor. I happen to lovee boxed cake mix, for the record! This cake, if done right, is incredibly fluffy, moist, adn tastes great!! Tips I followed: I beat the butter and sugar for several minutes until it was very light and fluffy! Like icing! Then I added each yolk one at a time and blended well. I didn't have cake flower so I used 2T corn starch per cup flour (in my case 4t to 2/3 cup). I sifted them into the a bowl, mixed with a whisk, and sifted (a second time) into the bowl with with the "wet" ingredients (also added flour FIRST). Yes all these things take extra time and effort and seem as though they couldn't make much of a difference, but that's baking, and they really do! TRY THIS :)

text:
This is an excellent yellow cake recipe! I have made many from-scratch cakes and this is one of the moistest and most delicious I've ever tasted. As some reviewers have stated, it is critical that you follow the directions carefully. You must take your time beating the sugar with the butter and how you incorporate your eggs. The only change I made to the original recipe was to substitute buttermilk for the regular milk (I had buttermilk on hand).I also baked it in 9 inch rounds making sure to watch the carefully rather than relying on time alone. This cake stayed moist for a week. Even the exposed cut sides stayed moist just covered with plastic wrap. I will definitely be making this cake again!

I used this recipe for a birthday cake for work, and it got rave reviews. It came out moist, with good texture, and great taste. My only tips would be sift the dry ingredients twice as another reviewer said, and scoop the flour into the measuring cup with a spoon, rather than using the cup directly. This will prevent it getting packed down, and keep you from using too much flour.

Delish!!!! This is hands down one of the best cake recipes ever! I made a few changes. I didn't have cake flour so I took out 2T of flour & added 2T of cornstarch. I sifted all the dry ingrediants twice and made sure to cream the sugar & butter for at least 5 mins. I did 2t of vanilla and I did 4 eggs (so my cake wasn't really yellow!) which I added the yolks 1 at a time & then added the whites which had been lightly beaten. I have made both cupcakes & 1/4 sheet cake. Both recieved rave reviews by family & friends! This will be my go to cake recipe from now on! Thank you!!!

text:
This is a very good yellow cake. The consistency and moistness of the cake is perfect. Smell the batter just before you pour it. It smells heavenly! Be aware that the batter will be thick; you really have to spread it after pouring into your pans. It bakes up nicely though. The reason why I give this four stars is because there is something a bit off with the taste. You can really taste the eggs in the cake. This isn't exactly a bad thing, but it is a bit much for my and my husband's taste. Perhaps we just aren't used to a yellow cake made from scratch. I followed the recipe exactly. I made sure to cream my eggs and sugar very well and let the eggs and butter sit to room temp. I have read others say that they used four whole eggs instead of eight egg yolks. Perhaps, this will work better; I will probably try this next time. However, if I do this it will be a white cake. Cakes using only the egg yolk are yellow and cakes with the whole egg are white. Anyway, I do not want to deter anyone here. It does go great with chocolate frosting. I'm just not sure If I would bring this to a dinner party. I admit that I am a bit of  a cake snob. I will continue my search for the perfect yellow cake.

text:
I made this cake for my daughter's 5th birthday. She asked for a castle cake. This recipe calls for a lot of egg yolks but now I know the reason. It's quite a delicious and moist cake. I doubled the recipe (used this cake for the castle base) and used 9 x 13" pan. The cake turned out well but I have to remember to invert cake onto a cake board instead of cooling rack as cake broke apart a bit. Not to worry though, easy to fix with icing. I didn't find the cake to be dry, a bit dense but just what I needed. You need to make sure to follow recipe and when cake top springs back or stick inserted to middle of cake comes out clean (this is what I did) remove from oven (prevents dry cake). Definitely better than store bought, packed yellow cake. I will use this recipe again. My daughter thinks this cake is very yummy and she knows cake!

country:
None
text:
I bake all of the time, but this was my first homemade yellow cake. I used this recipe with a few adjustments: 3 whole eggs, 2 yolks, lowfat buttermilk instead of just milk. I made cupcakes, and they turned out alright. You definitely need to make sure you leave it in the oven until the tops turn slightly brown or the centers will be full of eggs and flour. The cupcakes sunk quite a bit, unfortunately. It was still rather moist, though. I'll try this recipe once more and hope for the best.  My suggestions: use only 4 whole eggs, use the buttermilk alternative, realllyyyy beat the sugar and butter (with a beater, not your kitchenaid or it will stay at the bottom of the bowl while you add the other ingredients and won't mix well enough into the batter). Fill cupcake liners 3/4 full.

It's been awhile since I made a cake from scratch, but I'm looking for a great one. I followed this recipe to the letter, except I used 9" pans instead of 8" (that's what I have).  I'm not sure how people can say this cake is dense. My cake came out super light and fluffy. I actually wanted it to be a little denser LOL! I felt like it was just so "airy" in my mouth. Personally, I like my cake to be just a bit heavier so I feel like I'm eating something.  I used all the ingredients in the recipe and sifted the flour as stated once. I baked it for 25 minutes exactly. I give it 4 stars because it is definitely light in texture. It is a bit dry though.

text:
We have egg and milk allergies, so I substitute some things. I use allergy-safe margarine and milk, and use 4 Tbs of flax seed meal with 12 Tbs hot water in place of the 8 eggs. You need to reduce the butter/marg by a tablespoon or so because of the slight oil content of the flax. The cake turns out light and the crust is crispy. It has a great flavor and I eat it without frosting sometimes! (I would rather eat just frosting than just cake) We love this recipe.

Great recipe thank you David!

text:
This recipe is the best yellow cake I've ever made. It is very moist, delicious, and soft. It's a great way to get rid of frozen egg yolks. I split the recipe between a 9x9 and 8in. round pan (I frosted one and left the other bare). Beware! The cake is very soft and can easily break apart when being taken out of the pan. I found the round pan cake to be much easier to handle w/o breaking. This is a perfect recipe for entertaining as it will impress all your guests.
